### Post by Mark76 on 2010-08-01
Rules:

1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

And here's mine

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4099/4848151015_a94c78a12c.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4099/4848151015_a94c78a12c_b.jpg")

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4077/4848151525_e9f7ff45a6.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4077/4848151525_e9f7ff45a6_b.jpg")

### Post by PhilGil on 2010-08-01
> **dejan034 said:**
> 
Very nice..:)Thanks!

> **SagnaB said:**
> I don't understand. What is the point of this thread?

Please excuse my ignorance.
One of the neat things about Linux is how easy it is to customize your work environment; this thread gives visitors a chance to see for themselves.
Some folks put a lot of work into their customizations; this is a harmless way for them to show off.
Some desktops in these threads are real works of art and I enjoy seeing them.

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-08-02
> **proxess said:**
> I've never been able to get breadcrumbs to work. Can someone help me out?

You need nautilus elementary... [How to install Nautilus Elementary in Lucid]("http://www.omgubuntu.co.uk/2010/04/nautilus-elementary-230-for-lucid-gets.html")

Then follow the instructions on [this page]("http://www.webupd8.org/2010/04/nautilus-elementary-breadcrumbs-for-any.html") to install the breadcrumbs hack.

### Post by koleoptero on 2010-08-02
Why does everyone use the forums attachments for images? It resizes them and they look ugly. It'd be much nicer if you used an external host. I use omploader.org which even provides the thumbnailed bbcode ready to use. That way we can see all the details (and it doesn't even require you to register).

---

### Post by TheWeakSleep on 2010-08-03
> **markbahnman said:**
> Pretty cool setup there, what's the matrix thing in your third screenshot by the way?

Thanks, it's a small program called cmatrix. I use it as sort of a "screensaver" for my terminal, it starts as soon as i open my terminal, but as soon as i press any key it disappears :p

sudo apt-get install cmatrix

then just add cmatrix -s to somewhere in your .bashrc (theres *probably* a more elegant way to do it then just throwing it in there, but it was just a quick little thing and i just made it the first line :p)

---

### Post by markbahnman on 2010-08-03
> **TheWeakSleep said:**
> Thanks, it's a small program called cmatrix. I use it as sort of a "screensaver" for my terminal, it starts as soon as i open my terminal, but as soon as i press any key it disappears :p

sudo apt-get install cmatrix

then just add cmatrix -s to somewhere in your .bashrc (theres *probably* a more elegant way to do it then just throwing it in there, but it was just a quick little thing and i just made it the first line :p)
Many thanks! Found a cool fork of it in the AUR (I use arch) that I'm gonna try to setup as my desktop background.

### Post by El_Belgicano on 2010-08-04
> **jfreak_ said:**
> Nice.
Could you post your conky.rc and rc.xml

Reminder: [*_Screenshot_*]("http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=165388&d=1280869277")

Sure, my rc.xml is still not 100% done, I'm looking for some more useful keybindings/app-rules to make me less dependant of devilspie. Here you go:

**.conkyrc** (time&weather, using [Kaivalagi's: Conky Weather Forecast Python Script]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=869328"))
```
background yes

use_xft yes
xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=10
xftalpha 1.0

update_interval 15

total_run_times 0

own_window no
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_colour a6b38d
own_window_hints undecorated,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below

double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 200 20

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Draw borders around graphs
draw_graph_borders yes

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 1

# border width
border_width 0

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color blue
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black


# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 50
gap_y 50

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

use_spacer none

# Allow each port monitor to track at most this many connections (if 0 or not set, default is 256)
#max_port_monitor_connections 256

# Maximum number of special things, e.g. fonts, offsets, aligns, etc.
#max_specials 512

# Maximum size of buffer for user text, i.e. below TEXT line.
#max_user_text 16384

text_buffer_size 1024

TEXT
${color #708090}${font Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=50}${alignc}${time %H:%M}${font}
${voffset -5}${hr 1}
${font Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=15}${alignc}${time %d %B %G}${font}







${execpi 300 conkyForecast --location=BEXX0008 --template=/home/thomas/.conkyForecast.template}
```

**.conkyForecast.template** (used by .conkyrc)
```
[--datatype=CN], [--datatype=CO]
${voffset -10}${hr 1}
${font Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:style=Bold:size=15}[--datatype=CT]${font}
${voffset 10}Temp: [--datatype=HT --centeredwidth=3]
Humidity: [--datatype=HM]
Wind: [--datatype=WS]
${hr 1}
${alignc}[--datatype=DW --startday=1 --shortweekday]      [--datatype=DW --startday=2 --shortweekday]      [--datatype=DW --startday=3 --shortweekday]
${font ConkyWeather:size=26}${alignc}[--datatype=WF --startday=1]    [--datatype=WF --startday=2]    [--datatype=WF --startday=3]${font}
${alignc}[--datatype=LT --startday=1 --centeredwidth=3]     [--datatype=LT --startday=2 --centeredwidth=3]     [--datatype=LT --startday=3 --centeredwidth=3]
${alignc}[--datatype=HT --startday=1 --centeredwidth=3]     [--datatype=HT --startday=2 --centeredwidth=3]     [--datatype=HT --startday=3 --centeredwidth=3]
${hr 1}
${font Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=7}${voffset -10}${alignr}[--datatype=LU]

${alignr}${offset -80}${voffset -195}${font ConkyWeather:style=Bold:size=45}[--datatype=WF]${font}
```

**.conkyrcmpd** (only visible when mpd is in play/pause status)
```
background no

use_xft yes
xftfont Comic Sans MS:size=36
xftalpha 1.0

update_interval 1.0

total_run_times 0

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_hints undecorated,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_colour 708090

double_buffer yes

minimum_size 1200 100
maximum_width 1200

draw_shades no

draw_outline no

alignment bottom_left
gap_x 40
gap_y 60

draw_borders no
border_inner_margin 0
border_outer_margin 0
border_width 0

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer none
text_buffer_size 256

TEXT
${if_mpd_playing}${color #708090}${goto 10}${mpd_artist}
${font Comic Sans MS:size=22}${goto 40}${voffset -15}${mpd_title}
${alignr}${font Comic Sans MS:size=12}${mpd_status} (${mpd_elapsed}/${mpd_length})
${alignc}${mpd_bar 10,1000}${endif}
```

**.conkyrcsys** (make use of if-statements to display network information)
```
background yes

use_xft yes
xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans Mono:size=8
xftalpha 1.0

update_interval 1

total_run_times 0

own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_colour a6b38d
own_window_hints undecorated,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below

double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 1280 10

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Draw borders around graphs
draw_graph_borders yes

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 1

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color blue
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color black


# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment bottom_center

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 0
gap_y 0

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

use_spacer left

# Allow each port monitor to track at most this many connections (if 0 or not set, default is 256)
#max_port_monitor_connections 256

# Maximum number of special things, e.g. fonts, offsets, aligns, etc.
#max_specials 512

# Maximum size of buffer for user text, i.e. below TEXT line.
#max_user_text 16384

text_buffer_size 1024

TEXT
${alignc}${color #708090}<  Cpu: ${cpu}%  |  Temp: ${execi 1 cat /proc/acpi/thermal_zone/THRM/temperature | cut -c26-27}°C  |  Ram: ${memperc}%  |  Swap: ${swapperc}%  |  ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}Wired: -Down: ${totaldown eth0} (${downspeedf eth0}kbps) -Up:${totalup eth0} (${upspeedf eth0}kbps)  |  ${endif}${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth1/operstate up}Wireless: -Down:${goto 550}${totaldown eth1} (${downspeedf eth1}kbps) -Up:${totalup eth1} (${upspeedf eth1}kbps)  |  ${endif}Connections: ${tcp_portmon 1 65535 count}  >
```

**rc.xml** (includes some 'test' parts under app-rules and also 'not working' parts also under app-rules, xprop is killing me :p but  I keep looking...)
```
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<openbox_config xmlns="http://openbox.org/3.4/rc">
  <resistance>
    <strength>15</strength>
    <screen_edge_strength>25</screen_edge_strength>
  </resistance>
  <focus>
    <focusNew>yes</focusNew>
    <followMouse>no</followMouse>
    <focusLast>yes</focusLast>
    <underMouse>no</underMouse>
    <focusDelay>200</focusDelay>
    <raiseOnFocus>no</raiseOnFocus>
  </focus>
  <placement>
    <policy>Smart</policy>
    <center>yes</center>
    <monitor>Active</monitor>
    <primaryMonitor>1</primaryMonitor>
  </placement>
  <theme>
    <name>SlateVille</name>
    <titleLayout>NLIMC</titleLayout>
    <keepBorder>no</keepBorder>
    <animateIconify>no</animateIconify>
    <font place="ActiveWindow"><name>sans</name><size>8</size><weight>bold</weight><slant>normal</slant></font>
    <font place="InactiveWindow"><name>sans</name><size>8</size><weight>bold</weight><slant>normal</slant></font>
    <font place="MenuHeader"><name>sans</name><size>9</size><weight>normal</weight><slant>normal</slant></font>
    <font place="MenuItem"><name>sans</name><size>9</size><weight>normal</weight><slant>normal</slant></font>
    <font place="OnScreenDisplay"><name>sans</name><size>9</size><weight>bold</weight><slant>normal</slant></font>
  </theme>
  <desktops>
    <number>1</number>
    <firstdesk>1</firstdesk>
    <names></names>
    <popupTime>0</popupTime>
  </desktops>
  <resize>
    <drawContents>yes</drawContents>
    <popupShow>Nonpixel</popupShow>
    <popupPosition>Center</popupPosition>
    <popupFixedPosition>
      <x>10</x>
      <y>10</y>
    </popupFixedPosition>
  </resize>
  <margins>
    <top>30</top>
    <bottom>0</bottom>
    <left>0</left>
    <right>0</right>
  </margins>
  <dock>
    <position>TopLeft</position>
    <floatingX>0</floatingX>
    <floatingY>0</floatingY>
    <noStrut>no</noStrut>
    <stacking>Below</stacking>
    <direction>Vertical</direction>
    <autoHide>no</autoHide>
    <hideDelay>300</hideDelay>
    <showDelay>300</showDelay>
    <moveButton>Middle</moveButton>
  </dock>
  <keyboard>
    <chainQuitKey>C-g</chainQuitKey>
    <keybind key="W-space"><action name="ToggleShowDesktop"/></keybind>
    <keybind key="A-F4"><action name="Close"/></keybind>
    <keybind key="A-Tab"><action name="NextWindow"/></keybind>
    <keybind key="XF86AudioPrev"><action name="Execute"><command>mpc prev</command></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="XF86AudioNext"><action name="Execute"><command>mpc next</command></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="XF86AudioPlay"><action name="Execute"><command>mpc toggle</command></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="XF86AudioStop"><action name="Execute"><command>mpc stop</command></action></keybind>
		<keybind key="XF86AudioRaiseVolume"><action name="Execute"><execute>amixer sset Master 5%+</execute></action></keybind>
  	<keybind key="XF86AudioLowerVolume"><action name="Execute"><execute>amixer sset Master 5%-</execute></action></keybind>
  	<keybind key="XF86AudioMute"><action name="Execute"><execute>amixer sset Master toggle</execute></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="XF86WWW"><action name="Execute"><command>firefox</command></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="XF86Mail"><action name="Execute"><command>thunderbird</command></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="Print"><action name="Execute"><execute>scrot /home/thomas/'%Y-%m-%d-desktop.jpeg' -d 1 -q 80</execute></action></keybind>
    <keybind key="A-Escape"><action name="Lower"/><action name="FocusToBottom"/><action name="Unfocus"/></keybind>
  </keyboard>
  <mouse>
    <dragThreshold>15</dragThreshold>
    <doubleClickTime>200</doubleClickTime>
    <screenEdgeWarpTime>0</screenEdgeWarpTime>
    <context name="Frame">
      <mousebind button="A-Left" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Left" action="Click"><action name="Unshade"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Left" action="Drag"><action name="Move"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Right" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/><action name="Unshade"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Right" action="Drag"><action name="Resize"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Middle" action="Press"><action name="Lower"/><action name="FocusToBottom"/><action name="Unfocus"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Up" action="Click"><action name="DesktopPrevious"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-Down" action="Click"><action name="DesktopNext"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="C-A-Up" action="Click"><action name="DesktopPrevious"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="C-A-Down" action="Click"><action name="DesktopNext"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-S-Up" action="Click"><action name="SendToDesktopPrevious"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="A-S-Down" action="Click"><action name="SendToDesktopNext"/></mousebind>
    </context>
    <context name="Titlebar">
      <mousebind button="Left" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Left" action="Drag"><action name="Move"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Left" action="DoubleClick"><action name="ToggleMaximizeFull"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Middle" action="Press"><action name="Lower"/><action name="FocusToBottom"/><action name="Unfocus"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Up" action="Click"><action name="Shade"/><action name="FocusToBottom"/><action name="Unfocus"/><action name="Lower"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Down" action="Click"><action name="Unshade"/><action name="Raise"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Right" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/><action name="ShowMenu"><menu>client-menu</menu></action></mousebind>
    </context>
    <context name="Top">
      <mousebind button="Left" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/><action name="Unshade"/></mousebind>
      <mousebind button="Left" action="Drag"><action name="Resize"><edge>top</edge></action></mousebind>
    </context>
    <context name="Left">
      <mousebind button="Left" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/></mousebind>

    </context>
    <context name="Right">
      <mousebind button="Left" action="Press"><action name="Focus"/><action name="Raise"/></mousebind>

### Post by schreber on 2010-08-04
> **ScarletWyvern said:**
> The album art was tricky to set up, but I think it was worth it. : D

Thoughts?
Mind sharing how you did it? Not many people would go to such lengths for for album art but it definitely make it unique.

---

### Post by ScarletWyvern on 2010-08-04
It's just a part of my conky script using the conkyBanshee script and ImageMagick.

```
${execi 15 cp "`conkyBanshee -d CA | sed -e 's/album-art/media-art/'`" /home/wyvern/.album.png}${execi 15 convert /home/wyvern/.album.png -resize 374x374\! - | composite -compose CopyOpacity /home/wyvern/.albummask - /home/wyvern/.album.png}${execi 15 convert /home/wyvern/.album.png -background '#00000000' -rotate -11.9 .album.png}${image /home/wyvern/.album.png -p 434,345 -n}
```

Considering I'd never really used ImageMagick before yesterday... Yeah. It gave me some trouble. 

conkyBanshee is a script I found somewhere here on these forums, though I don't remember exactly where.

### Post by jurialmunkey on 2010-08-05
Okay... Here it is for download.
Finally in a state that I like, still many tweaks todo though.
First time using UbuntuOne so hopefully the download works.

[Download Victorious-Elements]("http://ubuntuone.com/p/Bsf/")

Unzip to a folder.
Run "sudo ./install.sh" to install for all users.

<<- Included ->>
Three variations on Gtk-theme [Normal, Dark, Light]
Four Emerald Themes [3 Light + 1 Dark]
A Metacity theme [Still needs tweaking]
Two Wallpapers [Blue + Purple] (only 1280x1024 sorry)
A Gnome-panel image (only 1280x1024)
A monochrome icon set based off Faenza and Monochrome-Elementary

Nautilus sidebar bg_color = tooltip fg_color
Nautilus sidebar text color = tooltip bg color

<<- Suggested ->>
Docky w/ HUD theme
Covergloobus w/ twquet theme

[IMG]http://i73.photobucket.com/albums/i202/jurialmunkey/Screenshot-25resized.png[/IMG]

### Post by Sonybuntu on 2010-08-06
Okay, my desk changed on July 31, and I was too late to edit my post.

Desktop: its "earth-horizon.png" in /usr/share/backgrounds/cosmos
Theme: Pay attention, this is different.
```
GTK theme: Elementary
Window borders: Equinox
Icons: Faenza (really nice, don't you think?)
```
Dock: Docky, since I had a change of mind.
Conky: Conky-Colors (I suck at .conkyrc files. . .)
Font: Lucida Grande (OSX default font) set to 8.5, 8.5 bold for window title. To get the complete look, click details on fonts tab (in the appearance window) and set hinting to none.

[[IMG]http://img17.imageshack.us/img17/5046/deskaug.th.png[/IMG]](http://img17.imageshack.us/i/deskaug.png/)

### Post by markbahnman on 2010-08-07
Finally got around to trying to set up the urxvt background with cmatrix running. Still a few issues I'm working on in my setup. 

 [[IMG]http://img819.imageshack.us/img819/2275/201008070127461680x1050.th.png[/IMG]](http://img819.imageshack.us/img819/2275/201008070127461680x1050.png)

Made a short screencast of my desktop, oddly enough my CPU cores are currently only at 2%/8%, the 80% in the screencast is all from xvidcap.

[http://dl.dropbox.com/u/6348934/screencast.mpeg](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/6348934/screencast.mpeg)

Setup is basically gutterslob's [BlueMono]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/post/72528/#p72528") theme, customized a bit. I plan on making it a heavily text based setup, trying to learn things like Vim and MC, switching to MoC and such.

The background terminal is selectable so I can't right-click on it to access my menu, thinking of trying to find a way to put a transparent layer just above the terminal or something. Also thinking of uninstalling LXDE and just going back to building things from the WM up.

To do it, btw, I basically followed [ArchWiki]("http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Openbox#Urxvt_in_the_background")'s instructions, adding this to my rc.xml
```
<application name="URxvt-bg">
  <decor>no</decor>
  <focus>no</focus>
  <position>
    <x>center</x>
    <y>20</y>
  </position>
  <layer>below</layer>
  <iconic>no</iconic>
  <skip_taskbar>yes</skip_taskbar>
  <skip_pager>yes</skip_pager>
  <desktop>all</desktop>
  <maximized>true</maximized> #Only if you want a full size terminal.
</application>
```And set the fonts and colors in .Xdefaults and set up this to run on startup
```
urxvt -name URxvt-bg +tr +sb -bl
```

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-08-07
> **ScarletWyvern said:**
> 
Woah. That looks pretty awesome. I've been considering getting a netbook soon, and I'm probably going to install #! or #! Lite on it. Mind letting me in on what you've got going on there?
It's just your basic Openbox session (mine's based on a Debian netinstall with Unstable and Liquorix kernel sources) with a lot of configs taken from a #! Statler setup. Openbox theme, GTK and wallpaper are home-brewed, panel is tint2 configured to match my theme, system monitor on left is conky.
Second screenshot is just terminator configured to run in multi-split mode (cos I'm a bit lazy to set up a screen.rc right now) with lots of reconfigured keybindings.
Fonts are Artwiz.

Haven't put out this theme yet, but there are some similar theme packs/suites available [here]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/post/72528/#p72528") and [here]("http://www.mediafire.com/?dtnikjnoebd") if you want em.



> **markbahnman said:**
> Finally got around to trying to set up the urxvt background with cmatrix running. Still a few issues I'm working on in my setup. 

 [[IMG]http://img819.imageshack.us/img819/2275/201008070127461680x1050.th.png[/IMG]]("http://img819.imageshack.us/img819/2275/201008070127461680x1050.png")

Made a short screencast of my desktop, oddly enough my CPU cores are currently only at 2%/8%, the 80% in the screencast is all from xvidcap.

.......
.......Nice work. 
I remember my CPU being a bit much more stressed back when I tried this. Was fun to use, but just couldn't get used to the idea of the cpu doing more work than necessary (especially when some of the graphic apps I use already put quite a strain on the system), and having to move the mouse over to tint or conky to get the right-click menu became a bit tiring after a while. You screencast is pure sex, though (makes the one I PMed you seem shitty by comparison... I blame that useless app I used to make it, forgot the name)

You get full marks for the geek-porn!! :)
Only thing I'd change are the fonts, though that's purely personal (I prefer pixel fonts for this sort of setup)

From the screenshot, I notice slight drop-shadowing on the fonts in the scrolling background, which tells me you have xcompmgr working.... might as well disable it since the backdrop is already equally dark and  the borders in the theme already do a reasonable job of separation between windows.

Made a short screencast of my desktop, oddly enough my CPU cores are currently only at 2%/8%, the 80% in the screencast is all from xvidcap.

[http://dl.dropbox.com/u/6348934/screencast.mpeg](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/6348934/screencast.mpeg)

Setup is basically gutterslob's [BlueMono]("http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/post/72528/#p72528") theme, customized a bit. I plan on making it a heavily text based setup, trying to learn things like Vim and MC, switching to MoC and such.

The background terminal is selectable so I can't right-click on it to access my menu, thinking of trying to find a way to put a transparent layer just above the terminal or something. Also thinking of uninstalling LXDE and just going back to building things from the WM up.

To do it, btw, I basically followed [ArchWiki]("http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Openbox#Urxvt_in_the_background")'s instructions, adding this to my rc.xml
```
<application name="URxvt-bg">
  <decor>no</decor>
  <focus>no</focus>
  <position>
    <x>center</x>
    <y>20</y>
  </position>
  <layer>below</layer>
  <iconic>no</iconic>
  <skip_taskbar>yes</skip_taskbar>
  <skip_pager>yes</skip_pager>
  <desktop>all</desktop>
  <maximized>true</maximized> #Only if you want a full size terminal.
</application>
```And set the fonts and colors in .Xdefaults and set up this to run on startup
```
urxvt -name URxvt-bg +tr +sb -bl
```

  Some useful settings for the urxvt terminal:
```
.Xdefault:
URxvt.shading:40
URxvt.inheritPixmaps:true
URxvt.transparent:true
URxvt.blurRadius:20x20
URxvt.fading:20
URxvt.visualBell:true
URxvt.scrollBar:true
URxvt.scrollBar_right:true
URxvt.scrollBar_floating:true
URxvt.cursorBlink:true
URxvt.jumpScroll:true
URxvt.skipScroll:true
URxvt.print-pipe:echo
URxvt.saveLines:5000
```
 :)

### Post by El_Belgicano on 2010-08-10
> **TheNerdAL said:**
> How would you minimize and maximize? :P

> **TheWeakSleep said:**
> The default keyboard shortcuts for minimize and maximize are Alt+F9 and Alt+F10 respectivley, I believe.

Don't remember, but if you know a bit about the rc.xml openbox file, you'll already know how easy it is to tweak the <keybindings> part, even if you don't want to use your keyboard to maximize, you could play with the mouse settings (again in rc.xml) to tell OB, for example, "right-clicking on the titlebar maximizes the window". Mouse actions are a bit trickier to make, but you could have a look at the defaults ones to see how they are made.

OB rules! rc.xml is freedom... ;)

---

### Post by DownTown22 on 2010-08-12
I've wondering what the next "thing" was going to be with desktops as the last few months have gotten somewhat (dare I say) stagnant with desktops.

The Compiz craze has come and gone, Conky's not as crazy as it used to be (besides on the Conky thread), docks aren't so crazy anymore - but they seem to be making a comeback with the latest AWN release and together with Docky, looking a lot more polished!.

It seems like the Faenza icon set is starting to take over desktops - I remember the days when you HAD to have Gnome-colors icon set (is it even still around?).

Just an observation on the desktop threads....no screenshot for me though, as my Ubuntu laptop has a dead screen.

---

### Post by schreber on 2010-08-12

If/When touchscreen monitors ever take off I can see something like the iOS/Android interface becoming a more standard approach to the desktop but I don't really see that happening until touchscreens reach astronomical size (20+" - think the iPad meets Goliath) and someone figures out a way to make things "just work" in that manner.

### Post by TheWeakSleep on 2010-08-12
@Cam! why do you say inspired from the iphone/mac community?

---

### Post by Cam! on 2010-08-12
> **TheWeakSleep said:**
> @Cam! why do you say inspired from the iphone/mac community?

Custom themes for Mac OS X and iOS vary, and are more artistic and well-done compared to the Windows/Windows Mobile/Android theme community. Apple-related themes usually look colorful, artistic, and in many times, insanely creative.

However, when it comes to Windows and Android, a majority of the themes and icons are just simple glossy, shiny, high-tech stuff, inspired by Alienware iconography. Boooring.

---

### Post by TheWeakSleep on 2010-08-12
Ahh I see what you're saying, though i probably would have said they are more similar to, not inspired from, the mac themes. I personally have seen many windows themes that aren't the shiny transparent ones that come by default, though i also haven't seen many mac themes to begin with. I do however think it's easier to make a mac look good than it is windows 7 :P

### Post by Frogs Hair on 2010-08-13
> **DownTown22 said:**
> What icon set and GTK theme is that?

Also, where did you get that equalizer from?

The icons are Tok tok V.3 some icons come as part  the GnoMenu  (Icon Menu 2). The theme is Cold Impression with some color modification (selected items and tool tips) Wall paper is from deviantArt and the dock icons are FeelinGrey. The equalizer is pulse audio and the instructions for the ppa download I found here in the Cafe . Just search Pulse Audio Equalizer and the thread should come up. The eq sounds great and all icons come from Gnome Look.org .

### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2010-08-14
It took a bit of work, but I finally jumped on the Faenza train. I had to symlink some icons for missing apps, pidgin's tray, and xfce power manager, then replace icons for gnome-gmail-notifier. After realizing that xfce's weather applet has zero themability, I switched to xfapplet + Weather Report to make it work. And then I shamelessly took the emblems from Gnome-Colors and put them in Faenza. Despite the different styles, they go together pretty decently. Faenza doesn't have an Arch icon yet, so I used one from AwOken. Monochrone panel icons are awesome. The dark action icons look slightly awkward with Shiki-style menus, but they don't look bad IMO, so I'm not messing with it.

GTK Theme: [Flow-Sublime](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=124681)[/shamelessplug] (to be updated soon)
Window Theme: Shiki-Colors
Icon Theme: Faenza
Font: Droid Sans 9
Wallpaper: [Abstract Vector Walls by Uribaani](http://uribaani.deviantart.com/art/Abstract-Vector-Walls-WP-Pack-61939400)

Clean:
[[img]http://omploader.org/tNTh0MA[/img]](http://omploader.org/vNTh0MA)
Not quite clean:
[[img]http://omploader.org/tNTh0Mg[/img]](http://omploader.org/vNTh0Mg)

### Post by logankoester on 2010-08-18
My new Multihead Ubuntu 10.04 workstation (Intel I7 quad)

Wallpaper from [InterfaceLift]("http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper_beta/downloads/date/any/")

**Applications**
Panel: [tint2]("http://code.google.com/p/tint2/")
Terminal: gnome-terminal
Editor: [GVIM2]("http://www.vim.org/")
Widgets: [screenlets]("http://screenlets.org/index.php/Home")
Dock: [Gnome-Do]("http://do.davebsd.com/") (modified to run on multiple X11 sessions)

[[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4116/4904533123_b593e89809.jpg[/IMG]]("http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4116/4904533123_b593e89809_b.jpg")

[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4081/4904531077_490fe89209_z.jpg[/IMG]
[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4121/4905120644_3ffe1feff0_z.jpg[/IMG]
[IMG]http://farm5.static.flickr.com/4121/4905120618_f64d25460c_z.jpg[/IMG]

It's a work in progress, but so far switching to 3 displays has been very worthwhile to give my programming productivity a boost. Rotating the center display allows me to view 100 lines of code on a page, while the left tails logfiles & autotest results, with documentation on the right.

I also use a free (commercial) product called Desktop Multiplier ([http://www.userful.com/products/userful-multiplier](http://www.userful.com/products/userful-multiplier)) which lets me plug in a second mouse/keyboard when my girl is here and needs something bigger than a netbook to use.

Since the displays are wall-mounted and I still have a DVI output available, I think the next step is going to be replacing the desk with a multitouch table, once Ubuntu's multitouch support begins to mature. They look like a lot of fun to build.

Thoughts?

---

### Post by TheNerdAL on 2010-08-18
> **logankoester said:**
> 
It's a work in progress, but so far switching to 3 displays has been very worthwhile to give my programming productivity a boost. Rotating the center display allows me to view 100 lines of code on a page, while the left tails logfiles & autotest results, with documentation on the right.

I also use a free (commercial) product called Desktop Multiplier ([http://www.userful.com/products/userful-multiplier](http://www.userful.com/products/userful-multiplier)) which lets me plug in a second mouse/keyboard when my girl is here and needs something bigger than a netbook to use.

Since the displays are wall-mounted and I still have a DVI output available, I think the next step is going to be replacing the desk with a multitouch table, once Ubuntu's multitouch support begins to mature. They look like a lot of fun to build.

Thoughts?

I am so jealous. :P

### Post by logankoester on 2010-08-19
> **TheNerdAL said:**
> I am so jealous. :P

A lot of people have been saying that to me, I don't think they realize just how cheap a system like this can be had.

The displays were like $160 each (27" 1080p), the wallmount arms were $30 from [Monoprice]("http://www.monoprice.com/home/index.asp"), dual-dvi graphics cards $80 each.

And yet my friends are still shelling out $1,799 for a 30" apple cinema display *facepalm*

### Post by logankoester on 2010-08-19
Ah yeah. Understandable :-)

It wouldn't have been worthwhile for a home desktop just to mess around with, I think. If you work at the machine it pays for itself.

On the other hand, it makes using a laptop or a smartphone SO much more painful on the road :lolflag:

---

### Post by logankoester on 2010-08-19
I'd actually recommend against dual, by the way. I've tried dual-head systems for a couple years, and I actually prefer only one.

The reason is that there is no center focal point. Stuff is either on the left or on the right, all the time, which is a really weird way to lay out your windows and can seriously hurt your neck after a few hours.  Also (depending on your WM & TwinView of course), maximizing a window draws it across both screens with a nice fat border in the middle. Very frustrating!

---

### Post by DjBones on 2010-08-19
I found a better background from wallbase.net, their abstract category has a lot of good stuff. To get the tabs into the status bar, I used the [buftabs.js](http://code.google.com/p/vimperator-labs/issues/detail?id=128) plugin for vimperator and changed a setting it details in the header to make the max tab length ten characters.

---

### Post by RiceMonster on 2010-08-19
> **logankoester said:**
> The reason is that there is no center focal point. Stuff is either on the left or on the right, all the time, which is a really weird way to lay out your windows and can seriously hurt your neck after a few hours.

Put one monitor in the center and another off to the side. Problem solved.

> **logankoester said:**
> Also (depending on your WM & TwinView of course), maximizing a window draws it across both screens with a nice fat border in the middle. Very frustrating!

I have yet to have that happen.

### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2010-08-19
Changed around quite a few things from my earlier post. Tweaked Flow some more. Added a desktop terminal and CoverGloobus. Installed Gloobus-Preview. ### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2010-08-19
> **fillintheblanks said:**
> nice how do you get the terminal like that
Use a terminal that supports either transparency or pseudo-transparency. I'm using Sakura here, but Gnome or Xfce terminals will work too. I prefer Sakura because it's lighter than both, and runs apart from my associated terminal.

Set it so that the background is completely see-through. Then find a good place to put it, and a size you like. Then you need to make it undecorated and sticky, and set it to skip the taskbar and pager. The final step will vary depending on your window manager. If you can tell me what window manager you're using, I can help you the rest of the way.

---

i noticed when i click the 'hide all window , Show desktop' button the conky minimises too. anyway to stop this ??

Looking good with the new Conky


Yeah, I've noticed that. It used to not do that, then I added some things. If there is a way to get it back, it will be in these settings probably: In fact it might even be the use_xft, because usually people have that set to no i I'm not mistaken. Let me know if that works, I haven't ever figured that part\icular thing out since last modifying it. 

[PHP]background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont 123:size=7
xftalpha 0.1

# set conky on the bottom of all other applications
on_bottom yes

update_interval 0.5
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 250 5
maximum_width 400
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
default_color gray
default_shade_color red
default_outline_color green
alignment top_right
gap_x 10
gap_y 10
no_buffers no
uppercase no
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 1
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer yes
text_buffer_size 256 [/PHP]

### Post by BslBryan on 2010-08-20
> **DownTown22 said:**
> Can I get your conky?
Here ya go. :-)

```
# conky configuration
#
# The list of variables has been removed from this file in favour
# of keeping the documentation more maintainable.
# Check http://conky.sf.net for an up-to-date-list.
#
# For ideas about how to modify conky, please see:
# http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/59/my-conky-config/
#
# For help with conky, please see:
# http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/2047/conky-help/
#
# Enjoy! :)
##############################################
#  Settings
##############################################
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=8
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
# Use Xft?
use_xft yes
xftfont Century Gothic:size=9
xftalpha 0.8
text_buffer_size 2048

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 60.0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
#own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 700 200

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Draw borders around graphs
draw_graph_borders no

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 3

# border margins
border_margin 9

# border width
border_width 1


alignment bottom_left


# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 120
gap_y 220

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
#override_utf8_locale no

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT


${font HandelGotD:size=100}${color ffffff}${execi 15 date +%I}$color${offset 10}:${execi 15 date +%M} $font ${voffset -105}${font HandelGotD:size=45}${color 000000}${execi 15 date +%d}$font ${voffset -48}${font HandelGotD:size=30}${color ffffff}${execi 15 date +%B}$font
${offset 300} ${voffset 10} ${font HandelGotD:size=45}${color 000000}${execi 15 date +%A}$font
```

### Post by BigCityCat on 2010-08-20
I tweeked the panel on this. This theme is Zuki Blues from deviant art. Wallpaper At deviant art/customization/wallpaper/in search box type ubuntu green and flip through a few pages. Then take to gimp and colorize and brightness and contast. 

For the theme copy the panel file and panel.rc from FFUU theme at gnome look and replace into Zuki Blues from deviant art. Drag and drop into appearance/themes.

Then follow the instructions from here for the panel.
[http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/ffuu?content=127731](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/ffuu?content=127731)

[IMG]http://i276.photobucket.com/albums/kk14/bigcitycat/Screenshot-4.png[/IMG]

### Post by mmesantos1 on 2010-08-22
> **cespinal said:**
> I can haz your conky configuration file? :D

Sure cespinal, here you go. 

> #avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
#own_window  yes
#own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_type normal
#own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 0
gap_y 27
alignment bottom_middle

#behaviour
update_interval 02

#colour
default_color  Grey

#default_shade_color 000000
own_window_colour 3d352a

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont gelly:pixelsize=11

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 875 0

TEXT
${alignc}Kernel: ${color Grey}$kernel   |  ${color} Up: ${color Grey}${uptime_short}   |   ${color}Cpu: ${color Grey}${cpu}%   ${color}${cpugraph 10,80 AEA08E 9F907D} ${color Grey}    |   ${color }Mem: ${color Grey}$mem/$memmax - $memperc% ${color} ${membar 8,80}${color Grey}    |   ${color }Net: ${color Grey}${font}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color}  ${downspeedgraph eth0 10,80 AEA08E 9F907D}  ${color Grey} ${totaldown eth0} down   |   ${color Grey}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color} ${upspeedgraph eth0 10,80 AEA08E 9F907D}  ${color Grey}${totalup eth0} up   |   ${alignc} ${color }Root: ${color Grey}${font}${fs_free /}  / ${fs_size /} - ${fs_free_perc /}%

### Post by mmesantos1 on 2010-08-24
> **Delvien said:**
> Conky config plox!


#avoid flicker
double_buffer yes

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
#own_window  yes
#own_window_transparent yes
#own_window_type normal
#own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 0
gap_y 27
alignment top_middle

#behaviour
update_interval 02

#colour
default_color  Grey

#default_shade_color 000000
own_window_colour 3d352a

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont gelly:pixelsize=11

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer no
minimum_size 875 0

TEXT
${alignc}Kernel: ${color Grey}$kernel   |  ${color} Up: ${color Grey}${uptime_short}   |   ${color}Cpu: ${color Grey}${cpu}%   ${color}${cpugraph 10,80 AEA08E 9F907D} ${color Grey}    |   ${color }Mem: ${color Grey}$mem/$memmax - $memperc% ${color} ${membar 8,80}${color Grey}    |   ${color }Net: ${color Grey}${font}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color}  ${downspeedgraph eth0 10,80 AEA08E 9F907D}  ${color Grey} ${totaldown eth0} down   |   ${color Grey}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s ${color} ${upspeedgraph eth0 10,80 AEA08E 9F907D}  ${color Grey}${totalup eth0} up   |   ${alignc} ${color }Root: ${color Grey}${font}${fs_free /}  / ${fs_size /} - ${fs_free_perc /}%

### Post by lee shore on 2010-08-24
> **spyd4r said:**
> how do you colour the bar in snow leopard?


You could use Themepark 3 ans 4 to changes most of the visual art files (panel, windows deco. but TP has a learning curve and can take some time to master.

Or you can use an installer with many themes on Deviantart and Macthemes. I am using a theme called SOG for SL
[http://macthemes.net/forum/viewtopic.php?id=16801420](http://macthemes.net/forum/viewtopic.php?id=16801420)

Changing fonts is done by a small porting tool and fontlabs.

### Post by Delvien on 2010-08-24
> **cespinal said:**
> Oh you..... 

Can I have your tint2 config?

I changed it a little since i posted that, but all you have to do is changed the border settings and poof

```
 #---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #000000 0
border_color = #D3CAAA 20

rounded = 4
border_width = 1
background_color = #D3CAAA 100
border_color = #35332A 100

rounded = 0
border_width = 0
background_color = #D3CAAA 0
border_color = #35332A 40

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
panel_position = center left vertical
panel_size = 99% 40
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 7 0
font_shadow = 1
panel_background_id = 1
wm_menu = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
#taskbar_mode = multi_desktop
taskbar_mode = single_desktop
taskbar_padding = 2 3 2
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 1
task_text = 0
task_width = 140
task_centered = 1
task_padding = 6 3
task_font = sans 7
task_font_color = #ffffff 70
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 85
task_background_id = 9
task_active_background_id = 2

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
systray_padding = 0 10 1
systray_background_id = 1


#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = sans 8
time2_format =%d %B
time2_font = sans 6
clock_font_color = #D3CAAA 100
clock_padding = 1 0
clock_background_id = 0
clock_lclick_command = 
clock_rclick_command = orage

#---------------------------------------------
# BATTERY
#---------------------------------------------
battery = 1
battery_low_status = 10
battery_low_cmd = notify-send "battery low"
bat1_font = sans 8
bat2_font = sans 6
battery_font_color = #D3CAAA 100
battery_padding = 1 0
battery_background_id = 0

# TOOLTIPS
#---------------------------------------------
tooltip = 1
tooltip_padding = 1 1
tooltip_show_timeout = 0
tooltip_hide_timeout = 0.5
tooltip_background_id = 2
tooltip_font = Droid Sans Bold 9
tooltip_font_color = #35332A 100



```

---

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-08-25
> **Delvien said:**
> What file manager is that? Are you using a gtk theme in obox? details ! : )
Like daniel stated, it's Thunar (pathbar and sidepane disabled)
...and yes, it's a GTK I'm working on, though I'm not really happy with it and might start on something else. [rant]I dunno, anything remotely light or mid-toned with shiny buttons just isn't my thing these days. I'd stick to my usual dark themes if I could successfully .css override every single webpage out there with a single script.[/rant]

Other details:
Font = Monte Carlo.pcf (linked below)
Icons = [Any Color You Like]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=102435") 
That should be it, I think.... just ask if you need anything else.


> **cespinal said:**
> awright.... Tint2 and Conky config pl0x :D

### Post by El_Belgicano on 2010-08-26
Hi everyone, any OpenBox guru to have a look at some weird happening? >[*_POST_*]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9764232&postcount=4")

And to stay on-topic:
- WM: OpenBox
- Icons: "Vamox" (battery is from "elementary" though)
- Themes: Slateville (OB and GTK)
- Wallpaper: "Tron Legacy" [(wallbase.net)]("http://www.wallbase.net")
- On screen: tint2, conky (conkyForecast by Kaivalagi, mpd+system info all gathered from the conky thread, I'm trying out cairo/lua these days...), ncmpc++ (front-end for MPD)

Will stay like this for a while now... (unless some workable answers to my post in the [*_Openbox Random Chatter II_*]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=930569"))

### Post by gutterslob on 2010-08-27
> **na12 said:**
> Is this openbox,what are you using to tile windows?Yes, it is Openbox.

That's actually just a single terminal, Terminator, split up. You cat set your own keybindings to split, resize, switch, etc quite easily in Terminator's preferences. Not 'pure' tiling, but if I dedicate an entire workspace to Terminator, I get a good balance between my GUI and CLI workflow.

There are a few apps you can use to get tiling in Openbox. I prefer [PtTyle]("http://pytyle.com/wiki/Main_Page"), but tbh, I usually just log out and back into my DWM desktop if I want my windows tiled (which I must admit is not very often these days).

Hope this helps.

Cheers.

---

### Post by mmesantos1 on 2010-08-28
> **maddbaron said:**
> very nice, conky please?

Thank you, here is the conkyrc. 

> background yes
use_xft yes
xftfONt Utopia:size=10
xftalpha 0.8
update_interval 2
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1
default_color white
default_shade_color black
alignment bottom_middle
gap_y 70
use_spacer no
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes

TEXT
${color white}$hr
${alignc}${color white}$kernel ${color darkgrey}ON ${color white}$nodename ${color white}
${alignc}${color white}${cpu cpu1}%${color darkgrey} CPU1 LOAD ${color white} ||  ${color white}${cpu cpu2}%${color darkgrey} CPU2 LOAD ${color white}
${alignc}${color white}$mem/$memmax ${color darkgrey}MEMORY USAGE || ${color white}$swap/$swapmax ${color darkgrey}SWAP USAGE
${alignc}${color white} $processes ${color darkgrey}processes ${color white} || ${color darkgrey}TOP PROCESS${color white} ${top name 1}
${alignc}${color white} ${fs_used /}${color darkgrey} of ${color white}${fs_size /}${color darkgrey} USED ON ${color white}/${color white} || ${alignc}${color white} ${fs_used /home}${color darkgrey} of ${color white}${fs_size /home}${color darkgrey} USED ON ${color white}/home${color white} || ${alignc}${color white} ${fs_used /media}${color darkgrey} of ${color white}${fs_size /media}${color darkgrey} USED ON ${color white}/media
${alignc}${color darkgrey} CONNECTED TO ${color white}${addr eth0} ${color white}
$hr

### Post by arzali on 2010-08-30
> **jorrieboy said:**
> What are the firefox add ons you use to let it look like that? And how did you get ubuntu forums to look like that (I have the human style, and i don't know how to change it)

addons are: hide menubar, apptabs and stylish.

styles i use:

TabbsOnTop
```
@-moz-document url("chrome://browser/content/browser.xul")

{



.tabbrowser-strip

{

position:fixed;

top:0px;



width:100%!important;

z-index:0;



}



tab

{

-moz-user-select:-moz-none!important;

z-index:0!important;

-moz-border-radius-bottomleft: 0px!important;

}



.tabbrowser-strip .tabbrowser-tabs

{

width:100%!important;

}



.tab-drop-indicator-bar

{

position:fixed!important;

top:0px;

left:0px;

width:100%!important;

z-index:1;

}



window

{

padding-top:28px;

}





}


#main-window #content .tabbrowser-tabs {
margin-top:2px!important;
margin-bottom:5px!important;
}




.tabbrowser-tabs tab
{
border-left: 8px dashed black !important;
border-right: 1px dashed black!important;

margin-left: 1px !important;
margin-right: 1px !important;


}


.tabbrowser-tabs
{
-moz-appearance:none !important;

}

/*******************************************************/

/* SELECTED TAB can be any color but black */
.tabbrowser-tabs tab[selected="true"] 
{
 
opacity: .9 !important;
} 
/* SELECTED TAB hover can be any color but black */











/*//////////////////////////////////////////////////*/

.tabbrowser-tabs .tab-icon-image

{
 height: 16px !important;
 width: 16px !important;
}



```Personal toolbar
```



#urlbar[fission="fusion"] > #statusbar-icon[value="100"] { visibility: visible !important; }
/* Hide bookmark icons in the Personal Toolbar */
toolbarbutton.bookmark-item > .toolbarbutton-icon {
display: none; }
/*FF3*/#urlbar,.searchbar-textbox{-moz-appearance:none!important}



/*FF3*/.urlbar-icon{padding-right:0px!important}





/*Farbe Suchleiste ändern*/





/*Farbe Tab-Hintergrund, Downloadmanager-Fenster usw. ändern*/

window,

dialog,

wizard,

page

{background-color: #E6E6E6 !important;}





.searchbar-textbox{border-width:0px 0px 0px!important;min-height:15px!important}

.autocomplete-history-dropmarker{max-height:20px!important;/*FF3*/background:ThreeDFace!important}

.autocomplete-history-dropmarker,/*FF3*/.searchbar-engine-button{border:none!important;background-image:none!important}



/*FF3*/.searchbar-engine-button>hbox{min-height:15px!important;margin-bottom:-2px!important}



    /* Show Stop and Reload buttons smartly*/



    #stop-button[disabled] {    display: none;}



    #stop-button:not([disabled]) + #reload-button {

        display: none;

    }





toolbarbutton.bookmark-item>.toolbarbutton-menu-dropmarker { display: none !important; } 
#navigator-toolbox #nav-bar 
{
-moz-appearance: none !important;
background: #E3E3E3 !important;
}

 !important; }

}
```

### Post by arzali on 2010-08-31
> **karmila said:**
> I love the panel :D

What theme is it? and the components, please...

Thanks. Theme is elementary. i dont really know what components you mean but here are the panel icons and background i use. you need elementary icons installed before you zuse this theme
[http://dl.dropbox.com/u/2137781/elementary-bright-monochrome2.tar.gz](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/2137781/elementary-bright-monochrome2.tar.gz)

for white text use the panel-dark.rc in the elementary theme or replace the original with the attached panel.rc in the apps folder of the elementary theme

Panel.rc
```
style "elementary-panel"
{
    xthickness        = 1
    ythickness        = 0

    #bg_pixmap[NORMAL]    = "/Panel/panel-dark.png" # Disable for normal panel backgrounds.

    engine "pixmap"
    {
        image
        {
            function        = BOX
            recolorable        = TRUE
            state            = NORMAL
        }
        
        image
        {
            function        = BOX
            recolorable        = TRUE
            state            = PRELIGHT
            file            = "Panel/button-active.png"
            border            = { 2, 2, 0, 0 }
            stretch            = TRUE
        }
        
        image
        {
            function        = BOX
            recolorable        = TRUE
            state            = ACTIVE
            file            = "Panel/button-active.png"
            border            = { 2, 2, 0, 0 }
            stretch            = TRUE
        }

        image
        {
            function        = BOX
            recolorable        = TRUE
            state            = SELECTED
            file            = "Panel/button-active.png"
            border            = { 2, 2, 0, 0 }
            stretch            = TRUE
        }
 
        image
        {
            function        = BOX
            recolorable        = TRUE
            state            = INSENSITIVE
        } 

        image
        {
            function        = ARROW
            recolorable        = TRUE
            arrow_direction        = DOWN
        }
    }
}

style "elementary-panel-light"
{
    xthickness        = 1
    ythickness        = 0

    fg[NORMAL]    = @fg_color

    engine "murrine" {
        textstyle = 1
        roundness = 0
    }
}

style "elementary-panel-text"
{
    fg[NORMAL]    = "#fff"
    fg[PRELIGHT]    = "#5D5D5D"
    fg[ACTIVE]    = "#ffffff"
    text[NORMAL]    = "#ffffff"
    text[PRELIGHT]    = "#ffffff"
    text[ACTIVE]    = "#ffffff"
}

style "elementary-main-menu-text" = "elementary-panel-text"
{
    fg[PRELIGHT]    = "#ffffff"
    text[PRELIGHT]    = "#ffffff"
}


style "elementary-panel-buttons" = "elementary-panel"
{
    GtkButton    ::child-displacement-x    = 0
    GtkButton    ::child-displacement-y    = 0

    xthickness    = 4
    ythickness    = 0

    engine "pixmap"
    {
        
        image
        {
            function        = BOX
            recolorable        = TRUE
            state            = PRELIGHT
            file            = "Panel/button-hover.png"
            border            = { 2, 2, 0, 0 }
            stretch            = TRUE
        }
        
    }
}

style "elementary-panel-handle" 
{
    engine "pixmap"
    {    
        image
        {
        function     = HANDLE
        }    
 
    image
        {
            function     = HANDLE
        }
    }
}

widget "*PanelWidget*"            style "elementary-panel"
widget "*PanelApplet*"            style "elementary-panel"
widget "*fast-user-switch*"        style "elementary-panel"
widget "*CPUFreq*Applet*"        style "elementary-panel"
widget "*indicator-applet*"        style "elementary-panel"
class "PanelApp*"            style "elementary-panel"
class "PanelToplevel*"            style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*PanelToplevel*"        style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*notif*"            style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*Notif*"            style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*Tray*"            style "elementary-panel" 
widget_class "*tray*"            style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*computertemp*"        style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*Applet*Tomboy*"        style "elementary-panel"
widget_class "*Applet*Netstatus*"    style "elementary-panel"

# Fixes for tooltip text in some apps.
widget_class "*Notif*Beagle*"        style "elementary-panel-light"
widget_class "*Notif*Brasero*"        style "elementary-panel-light"

# XFCE panel theming.
widget "*Xfce*Panel*"            style "elementary-panel"
class "*Xfce*Panel*"            style "elementary-panel"

# Make sure panel text color doesn't change
widget_class "*Panel*MenuBar*"        style "elementary-main-menu-text"
widget_class "*Panel*<GtkMenuBar>*"    style "elementary-main-menu-text"
widget "*.clock-applet-button.*"    style "elementary-panel-text"
widget "*PanelApplet*"            style "elementary-panel-text"

# Panel buttons
widget_class "*Panel*GtkToggleButton"    style:highest "elementary-panel-buttons"
widget_class "*Panel*GtkButton"        style:highest "elementary-panel-buttons"

# Hide ugly handle
class "PanelAppletFrame"         style:highest "elementary-panel-handle"
```

### Post by aspiredfang on 2010-10-10
Here's my anime loving desktop <3 I like things simple and with lots of space in order to maximise Window room for development.

The media player is normally closed after creating a playlist within MPD but, I thought you would like to see the theme.

- Using OpenBox & xcompmgr
- "Elegant" GTK theme for internal window styling
- Tilda for terminal access
- Clearly conky for system summation
- A general "Code Geass" look and feel :)
- XFCE panel along the top.I am using a customized version of Xubuntu
- As file manager, nautilus with --no-desktop
* Now I just need a new icon set *slaps self*This system has the horsepower so, why not make work "aesthetically" please after all
